   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Immaculate Conception</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>

     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Catholic doctrine that Mary was conceived free from original sin
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the doctrine that Mary was free from original sin. For the conception of Jesus, see <a href="/wiki/Virgin_birth_of_Jesus" title="Virgin birth of Jesus">virgin birth of Jesus</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Immaculate Conception (disambiguation)">Immaculate Conception (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p>The <b>Immaculate Conception</b><sup id="cite_ref-Disambiguate_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disambiguate-1">[Notes 1]</a></sup> is a dogma of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> which states that <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Mary, mother of Jesus</a> has been free of <a href="/wiki/Original_sin" title="Original sin">original sin</a> from the moment of her <a href="/wiki/Conception_(biology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conception (biology)">conception</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds2012330_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds2012330-2">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Definition_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Definition-3">[Notes 2]</a></sup> It proved controversial in the Middle Ages, but was revived in the 19th century and was adopted as Church dogma when <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a> promulgated <i><a href="/wiki/Ineffabilis_Deus" title="Ineffabilis Deus">Ineffabilis Deus</a></i> in 1854. This followed <i><a href="/wiki/Ubi_primum_(Pius_IX,_1849)" title="Ubi primum (Pius IX, 1849)">Ubi primum</a></i>, a 1849 encyclical wherein Pius had asked the bishops for their opinions on the matter,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoley2002153_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoley2002153-4">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHillerbrand2012250_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHillerbrand2012250-5">[3]</a></sup> resulting in overwhelming support from the Church's hierarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoyle199635_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoyle199635-6">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Protestants rejected <i>Ineffabilis Deus</i> as an exercise in papal power and the doctrine itself as without foundation in Scripture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerringer2019507_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerringer2019507-7">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a>, although it reveres Mary in its liturgy, called on the Roman church to return to the faith of early centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeyendorff198190_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeyendorff198190-8">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The iconography of the Virgin of the Immaculate Conception shows her standing, with arms outstretched or hands clasped in prayer, and her feast day is 8 December.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarrely201440_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarrely201440-9">[7]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Doctrine">Doctrine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Doctrine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The Immaculate Conception of Mary is one of the four <a href="/wiki/Mariology" title="Mariology">Marian</a> dogmas of the Catholic Church, meaning that it is held to be a divinely revealed truth whose denial is <a href="/wiki/Heresy" title="Heresy">heresy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollinge2012133_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollinge2012133-10">[8]</a></sup> Defined by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Ineffabilis_Deus" title="Ineffabilis Deus">Ineffabilis Deus</a></i>, 1854, it states that Mary, through God's grace, was conceived free from the stain of <a href="/wiki/Original_sin" title="Original sin">original sin</a> through her role as the <a href="/wiki/Mother_of_God" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother of God">Mother of God</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollinge2012209_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollinge2012209-11">[9]</a></sup> </p> 
      <blockquote> 
       <p>We declare, pronounce, and define that the doctrine which holds that the most Blessed Virgin Mary, in the first instance of her conception, by a singular grace and privilege granted by Almighty God, in view of the merits of Jesus Christ, the Saviour of the human race, was preserved free from all stain of original sin, is a doctrine revealed by God and therefore to be believed firmly and constantly by all the faithful.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheed1958134â138_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheed1958134â138-12">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      </blockquote> 
      <p>While the Immaculate Conception asserts Mary's freedom from original sin, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">Council of Trent</a>, held between 1545 and 1563, had previously affirmed her freedom from personal sin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFastiggi2019455_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFastiggi2019455-13">[11]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1013635363">.mw-parser-output .sidebar{width:22em;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 1em;background:#f8f9fa;border:1px solid       <h3><span id="Anna.2C_mother_of_Mary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Anna,_mother_of_Mary">Anna, mother of Mary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Anna, mother of Mary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The mother of Mary is not a biblical character.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENixon200411_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENixon200411-14">[12]</a></sup> She first appears in the late 2nd-century <a href="/wiki/Protevangelium_of_James" class="mw-redirect" title="Protevangelium of James">Protevangelium of James</a>, which names her <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anne" title="Saint Anne">Anne</a>, probably from <a href="/wiki/Hannah_(biblical_figure)" title="Hannah (biblical figure)">Hannah</a>, the mother of the prophet <a href="/wiki/Samuel" title="Samuel">Samuel</a>. She and her husband, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joachim" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Joachim">Saint Joachim</a>, are infertile, but God hears their prayers for a child. So is Mary conceived and born, and, like Samuel, taken to <a href="/wiki/Presentation_of_Mary" title="Presentation of Mary">spend her childhood in the temple</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENixon200411â12_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENixon200411â12-15">[13]</a></sup> In the earliest texts, probably representing the original version, the conception occurs without <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sexual intercourse</a> between Anne and Joachim, but the story does not advance the idea of an immaculate conception.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShoemaker2016unpaginated_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShoemaker2016unpaginated-16">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_sin">Original sin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Original sin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Original_sin" title="Original sin">Original sin</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Original sin is the Christian doctrine that each human being is born in a state of sin inherited from the first man, Adam, who disobeyed God in eating the forbidden fruit (of knowledge of good and evil) and, in consequence, transmitted his sin and guilt by heredity to his descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> The doctrine was defined by <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</a> (354â430 AD).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiley200237_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiley200237-18">[16]</a></sup> Engaged in a controversy with the monk <a href="/wiki/Pelagius" title="Pelagius">Pelagius</a> over the question of whether infants could sin (Pelagius said they could not and therefore would not go to hell if unbaptised), he inserted original sin and the fall from grace into the story of the <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" title="Garden of Eden">Garden of Eden</a> and Paul's <a href="/wiki/Letter_to_the_Romans" class="mw-redirect" title="Letter to the Romans">Letter to the Romans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEObach200841_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEObach200841-19">[17]</a></sup> Augustine identified male semen as the means by which original sin was made heritable, leaving only Jesus Christ, conceived without semen, free of the sin passed down from Adam through the sexual act.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStortz200193â94_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStortz200193â94-20">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Anselm_of_Canterbury" title="Anselm of Canterbury">Anselm of Canterbury</a> challenged this identification in the 11th-century, defining original sin as "privation of the righteousness that every man ought to possess". <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> distinguished the supernatural gifts of Adam before the fall from what was merely natural, and said that it was the former that were lost, privileges that enabled man to keep his inferior powers in submission to reason and directed to his supernatural end. <a href="/wiki/Duns_Scotus" title="Duns Scotus">Duns Scotus</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_of_Ockham" title="William of Ockham">William of Ockham</a>, identified original sin with the loss of sanctifying grace. </p>
      <p> According to Catechism of the Catholic Church, </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>By yielding to the tempter, Adam and Eve committed a personal sin, but this sin affected the human nature that they would then transmit in a fallen state. It is a sin which will be transmitted ...by the transmission of a human nature deprived of original holiness and justice. and that is why original sin is called "sin" only in an analogical sense: it is a sin "contracted" and not "committed" - a state and not an act.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_formulation">Medieval formulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Medieval formulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lusenberg-Immaculata-1876.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Lusenberg-Immaculata-1876.jpg/220px-Lusenberg-Immaculata-1876.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="301" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Lusenberg-Immaculata-1876.jpg/330px-Lusenberg-Immaculata-1876.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Lusenberg-Immaculata-1876.jpg/440px-Lusenberg-Immaculata-1876.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2166" data-file-height="2964"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lusenberg-Immaculata-1876.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Altar of the Immaculata</i> by <a href="/wiki/Josef_Moroder-Lusenberg" title="Josef Moroder-Lusenberg">Joseph Lusenberg</a>, 1876. Saint Antony's Church, <a href="/wiki/Urtij%C3%ABi" title="UrtijÃ«i">UrtijÃ«i</a>, Italy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mary's <a href="/wiki/Sinlessness_of_Mary" title="Sinlessness of Mary">freedom from personal sin</a> was affirmed in the 4th century, but Augustine's argument that original sin was transmitted through sex raised the question of whether she could also be free of the sin of Adam.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollinge2012209_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollinge2012209-11">[9]</a></sup> The English ecclesiastic and scholar <a href="/wiki/Eadmer" title="Eadmer">Eadmer</a> (c.1060-c.1126) reasoned that it was possible in view of God's omnipotence and appropriate in view of Mary's role as <a href="/wiki/Mother_of_God" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother of God">Mother of God</a>: <i>Potuit, decuit, fecit</i>, "it was possible, it was fitting, therefore it was done;"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoyle199636â37_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoyle199636â37-22">[20]</a></sup> Interpretations of the doctrine of Immaculate Conception were the subject of intensive dispute between <a href="/wiki/Franciscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan">Franciscans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">Dominicans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECameron1996335_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECameron1996335-23">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bernard_of_Clairvaux" title="Bernard of Clairvaux">Bernard of Clairvaux</a> (1090â1153) and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> (1225â1274), among others, objected that if Mary were free of original sin at her conception then she would have no need of redemption, making Christ superfluous; they were answered by <a href="/wiki/Duns_Scotus" title="Duns Scotus">Duns Scotus</a> (1264â1308), who reasoned that </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>Christ was Mary's Redeemer more perfectly by preservative redemption in shielding her from original sin through anticipating and foreseeing the merits of his passion and death. This pre-redemption indicates a much greater grace and more perfect salvation.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>Nevertheless, it was not theological theory that initiated discussion of Mary's freedom from mankind's curse, but the celebration of her liturgy in the eleventh century, for the popular feast of her conception brought forth the objection that as normal human conception was sinful, to celebrate Mary's conception was to celebrate a sinful event.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoss2000126_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoss2000126-26">[24]</a></sup> Some held that no sin had occurred, for Anne had conceived Mary not through sex but by kissing her husband Joachim, and that Anne's father and mother had likewise been conceived, but <a href="/wiki/St_Bridget_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="St Bridget of Sweden">St Bridget of Sweden</a> (c.1303â1373) told how Mary herself had revealed to her in a vision that although Anne and Joachim conceived their daughter through sexual union, the act was sinless because it was free of sexual desire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolberg2018108â109_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolberg2018108â109-27">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1431 the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Basel" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Basel">Council of Basel</a> declared Mary's immaculate conception a "pious opinion" consistent with faith and Scripture; the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">Council of Trent</a>, held in several sessions in the early 1500s, made no explicit declaration on the subject but exempted her from the universality of original sin; and by 1571 the Pope's <a href="/wiki/Breviary" title="Breviary">Breviary</a> (prayerbook) set out an elaborate celebration of the Feast of the Immaculate Conception on 8 December.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds20124â5,_117_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds20124â5,_117-28">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ineffabilis_Deus"><i>Ineffabilis Deus</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ineffabilis Deus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the 16th and especially the 17th centuries there was a proliferation of Immaculatist devotion in Spain, leading the Habsburg monarchs to demand that the papacy elevate the belief to the status of dogma.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHernÃ¡ndez20196_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHernÃ¡ndez20196-29">[27]</a></sup> In France in 1830 <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Labour%C3%A9" title="Catherine LabourÃ©">Catherine LabourÃ©</a> (May 2, 1806 â December 31, 1876) saw a vision of Mary as the Immaculate Conception standing on a globe while a voice commanded her to have a medal made in imitation of what she saw.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMack2003_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMack2003-30">[28]</a></sup> LabourÃ©'s vision marked the beginning of a great 19th-century Marian revival.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoley200229_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoley200229-31">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1849 with the encyclical <a href="/wiki/Ubi_primum_(Pius_IX,_1849)" title="Ubi primum (Pius IX, 1849)">Ubi primum (Pius IX, 1849)</a>, Pope <a href="/wiki/Pius_IX" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius IX">Pius IX</a> asked the bishops of the church for their views on whether the doctrine should be defined as dogma: ninety percent of those who responded were supportive, and in 1854 the papal bull <i>Ineffabilis Deus</i> was promulgated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoley2002153_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoley2002153-4">[2]</a></sup> Despite the fact that a good deal of the support for the dogma came from France, and that it had been promoted by one his predecessors, <a href="/wiki/Hyacinthe-Louis_de_Qu%C3%A9len" title="Hyacinthe-Louis de QuÃ©len">Hyacinthe-Louis de QuÃ©len</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marie-Dominique-Auguste_Sibour" title="Marie-Dominique-Auguste Sibour">Marie-Dominique-Auguste Sibour</a>, Archbishop of Paris thought the Immaculate Conception "could be proved neither from the Scriptures nor from tradition"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaff1931unpaginated_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaff1931unpaginated-32">[30]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-Weber_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weber-33">[31]</a></sup> Nonetheless, despite any reservations, after its promulgation, Sibour published the decree in his diocese. In 1857, the Archbishop was assassinated by an interdicted priest who disagreed with Sibour's support of clerical celibacy and the recently defined dogma. </p>
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/Ineffabilis_Deus" title="Ineffabilis Deus">Ineffabilis Deus</a></i> found the Immaculate Conception in the Ark of Salvation (<a href="/wiki/Noah%27s_Ark" title="Noah's Ark">Noah's Ark</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jacob%27s_Ladder" title="Jacob's Ladder">Jacob's Ladder</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Burning_Bush" class="mw-redirect" title="Burning Bush">Burning Bush</a> at Sinai, the Enclosed Garden from the <a href="/wiki/Song_of_Songs" title="Song of Songs">Song of Songs</a>, and many more passages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManelli200835_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManelli200835-34">[32]</a></sup> From this wealth of support the pope's advisors singled out <a href="/wiki/Protoevangelium" class="mw-redirect" title="Protoevangelium">Genesis 3:15</a> as the basis for the Immaculate Conception: "The most glorious Virgin ... was foretold by God when he said to the serpent: 'I will put enmity between you and the woman,'"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManelli19946â7_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManelli19946â7-35">[33]</a></sup> a prophecy which reached fulfillment in the figure of the Woman in the <a href="/wiki/Revelation_of_John" class="mw-redirect" title="Revelation of John">Revelation of John</a>, crowned with stars and trampling the Dragon underfoot.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETwomey200873â74_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETwomey200873â74-36">[34]</a></sup> Luke 1:28, and specifically the phrase "full of grace" by which <a href="/wiki/Gabriel" title="Gabriel">Gabriel</a> greeted Mary, was another reference to her immaculate conception: "she was never subject to the curse and was, together with her Son, the only partaker of perpetual benediction."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGerman2001596_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGerman2001596-37">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to Hans J. Hillerbrand, <i>Ineffabilis Deus</i> was one of the pivotal events of the papacy of Pius, pope from 16 June 1846 to his death on 7 February 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHillerbrand2012250_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHillerbrand2012250-5">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Four years later Mary appeared to the young <a href="/wiki/Bernadette_Soubirous" title="Bernadette Soubirous">Bernadette Soubirous</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lourdes" title="Lourdes">Lourdes</a>, in southern France, to announce that she was the Immaculate Conception.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHammond2003602_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHammond2003602-38">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Feast_and_patronages">Feast and patronages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Feast and patronages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Quadrittu_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Quadrittu_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Quadrittu_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Quadrittu_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Quadrittu_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Quadrittu_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Quadrittu_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Quadrittu_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The procession of the <i>Quadrittu</i> of the Immaculate Conception taken on December 7 in <a href="/wiki/Saponara" title="Saponara">Saponara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Patronages_of_the_Immaculate_Conception" title="Patronages of the Immaculate Conception">Patronages of the Immaculate Conception</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_the_Immaculate_Conception" title="Feast of the Immaculate Conception">Feast of the Immaculate Conception</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The feast day of the Immaculate Conception is December 8.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarrely201440_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarrely201440-9">[7]</a></sup> Its celebration seems to have begun in the Eastern church in the 7th century and may have spread to Ireland by the 8th, although the earliest well-attested record in the Western church is from England early in the 11th.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoss2000124_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoss2000124-39">[37]</a></sup> It was suppressed there after the <a href="/wiki/Norman_Conquest" title="Norman Conquest">Norman Conquest</a> (1066), and the first thorough exposition of the doctrine was a response to this suppression.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoss2000124_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoss2000124-39">[37]</a></sup> It continued to spread despite strong theological objections<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoss2000128_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoss2000128-40">[38]</a></sup> (in 1125 <a href="/wiki/St_Bernard_of_Clairvaux" class="mw-redirect" title="St Bernard of Clairvaux">St Bernard of Clairvaux</a> wrote to Lyons Cathedral to express his surprise and concern that it had recently begun to be observed there),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoss2000126_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoss2000126-26">[24]</a></sup> but in 1477 <a href="/wiki/Sixtus_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Sixtus IV">Sixtus IV</a>, a Franciscan, placed it on the Roman calendar (i.e., list of Church festivals and observances).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManelli2008643_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManelli2008643-41">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pius_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius V">Pius V</a> suppressed the word "immaculate",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHernÃ¡ndez201938_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHernÃ¡ndez201938-42">[40]</a></sup> but following the promulgation of <i>Ineffabilis Deus</i> it was restored with the typically Franciscan phrase "immaculate conception" and given a formulary for the Mass, drawn largely from one composed for Sixtus IV, beginning "O God who by the Immaculate Conception of the Virgin...". <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManelli2008643â644_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManelli2008643â644-43">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By pontifical decree a number of countries are considered to be under the patronage of the Immaculate Conception. These include <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (including the old kingdoms and the present state), the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>. By royal decree under the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bragan%C3%A7a" class="mw-redirect" title="House of BraganÃ§a">House of BraganÃ§a</a>, she is the principal Patroness of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prayers_and_hymns">Prayers and hymns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Prayers and hymns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Missal" title="Roman Missal">Roman Missal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Rite" title="Roman Rite">Roman Rite</a> <a href="/wiki/Liturgy_of_the_Hours" title="Liturgy of the Hours">Liturgy of the Hours</a> naturally includes references to Mary's immaculate conception in the feast of the Immaculate Conception. An example is the antiphon that begins: "<a href="/wiki/Tota_pulchra_es" title="Tota pulchra es">Tota pulchra es, Maria, et macula originalis non est in te</a>" ("You are all beautiful, Mary, and the original stain [of sin] is not in you." It continues: "Your clothing is white as snow, and your face is like the sun. You are all beautiful, Mary, and the original stain [of sin] is not in you. You are the glory of Jerusalem, you are the joy of Israel, you give honour to our people. You are all beautiful, Mary.")<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> On the basis of the original <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_chant" title="Gregorian chant">Gregorian chant</a> music,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> polyphonic settings have been composed by <a href="/wiki/Anton_Bruckner" title="Anton Bruckner">Anton Bruckner</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Casals" title="Pablo Casals">Pablo Casals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Durufl%C3%A9" title="Maurice DuruflÃ©">Maurice DuruflÃ©</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grzegorz_Gerwazy_Gorczycki" title="Grzegorz Gerwazy Gorczycki">Grzegorz Gerwazy Gorczycki</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> <a href="https://no.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ola_Gjeilo" class="extiw" title="no:Ola Gjeilo">no:Ola Gjeilo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Maur%C3%ADcio_Nunes_Garcia" title="JosÃ© MaurÃ­cio Nunes Garcia">JosÃ© MaurÃ­cio Nunes Garcia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> and <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolaus_Schapfl" class="extiw" title="de:Nikolaus Schapfl">Nikolaus Schapfl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other prayers honouring Mary's immaculate conception are in use outside the formal liturgy. The <a href="/wiki/Immaculata_prayer" title="Immaculata prayer">Immaculata prayer</a>, composed by Saint <a href="/wiki/Maximillian_Kolbe" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximillian Kolbe">Maximillian Kolbe</a>, is a prayer of entrustment to Mary as the Immaculata.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Novena" title="Novena">novena</a> of prayers, with a specific prayer for each of the nine days has been composed under the title of the Immaculate Conception Novena.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ave_Maris_Stella" class="mw-redirect" title="Ave Maris Stella">Ave Maris Stella</a> is the vesper hymn of the feast of the Immaculate Conception.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> The hymn <i><a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Mary" title="Immaculate Mary">Immaculate Mary</a></i>, addressed to Mary as the Immaculately Conceived One, is closely associated with <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="Our Lady of Lourdes">Lourdes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistic_representation">Artistic representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Artistic representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Marian_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Marian art">Roman Catholic Marian art</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Giotto_-_Scrovegni_-_-06-_-_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Giotto_-_Scrovegni_-_-06-_-_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate.jpg/220px-Giotto_-_Scrovegni_-_-06-_-_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Giotto_-_Scrovegni_-_-06-_-_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate.jpg/330px-Giotto_-_Scrovegni_-_-06-_-_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Giotto_-_Scrovegni_-_-06-_-_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate.jpg/440px-Giotto_-_Scrovegni_-_-06-_-_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="694" data-file-height="676"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Giotto_-_Scrovegni_-_-06-_-_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Giotto, <i>Meeting at the Golden Gate</i>, 1304â1306
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Immaculate Conception became a popular subject in literature,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETwomey2008ix_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETwomey2008ix-56">[54]</a></sup> but its abstract nature meant it was late in appearing as a subject in art.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHall2018337_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHall2018337-57">[55]</a></sup> During the Medieval period it was depicted as "<a href="/wiki/Joachim_and_Anne_Meeting_at_the_Golden_Gate" title="Joachim and Anne Meeting at the Golden Gate">Joachim and Anne Meeting at the Golden Gate</a>", meaning Mary's conception through the chaste kiss of her parents at the Golden Gate in Jerusalem;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHall2018175_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHall2018175-58">[56]</a></sup> the 14th and 15th centuries were the heyday for this scene, after which it was gradually replaced by more allegorical depictions featuring an adult Mary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHall2018171_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHall2018171-59">[57]</a></sup> The 1476 extension of the <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_the_Immaculate_Conception" title="Feast of the Immaculate Conception">feast of the Immaculate Conception</a> to the entire Latin Church reduced the likelihood of controversy for the artist or patron in depicting an image, so that <a href="/wiki/Emblem" title="Emblem">emblems</a> depicting <i>The Immaculate Conception</i> began to appear. Many artists in the 15th century faced the problem of how to depict an abstract idea such as the Immaculate Conception, and the problem was not fully solved for 150 years. The Italian Renaissance artist <a href="/wiki/Piero_di_Cosimo" title="Piero di Cosimo">Piero di Cosimo</a> was among those artists <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception_(Piero_di_Cosimo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Immaculate Conception (Piero di Cosimo)">who tried new solutions</a>, but none of these became generally adopted so that the subject matter would be immediately recognisable to the faithful.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The definitive <a href="/wiki/Iconography" title="Iconography">iconography</a> for the depiction of "Our Lady" seems to have been finally established by the painter and theorist <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pacheco" title="Francisco Pacheco">Francisco Pacheco</a> in his "El arte de la pintura" of 1649: a beautiful young girl of 12 or 13, wearing a white tunic and blue mantle, rays of light emanating from her head ringed by twelve stars and crowned by an imperial crown, the sun behind her and the moon beneath her feet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoffitt2001676_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoffitt2001676-60">[58]</a></sup> Pacheco's iconography influenced other <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> artists or artists active in Spain such as <a href="/wiki/The_Immaculate_Conception_Paintings_by_El_Greco" class="mw-redirect" title="The Immaculate Conception Paintings by El Greco">El Greco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Murillo" class="mw-redirect" title="BartolomÃ© Murillo">BartolomÃ© Murillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez" title="Diego VelÃ¡zquez">Diego VelÃ¡zquez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Zurbar%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco ZurbarÃ¡n">Francisco ZurbarÃ¡n</a>, who each produced a number of artistic masterpieces based on the use of these same symbols.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKatzOrsi200198_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKatzOrsi200198-61">[59]</a></sup> The popularity of this particular representation of <i>The Immaculate Conception</i> spread across the rest of Europe, and has since remained the best known artistic depiction of the concept: in a heavenly realm, moments after her creation, the <a href="/wiki/Spirit" title="Spirit">spirit</a> of Mary (in the form of a young woman) looks up in awe at (or bows her head to) God. The moon is under her feet and a <a href="/wiki/Halo_(religious_iconography)" title="Halo (religious iconography)">halo</a> of twelve stars surround her head, possibly a reference to "a woman clothed with the sun" from Revelation 12:1â2. Additional imagery may include clouds, a golden light, and <a href="/wiki/Putti" class="mw-redirect" title="Putti">putti</a>. In some paintings the putti are holding <a href="/wiki/Lilium" title="Lilium">lilies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rose" title="Rose">roses</a>, flowers often associated with Mary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJenner20093â9_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJenner20093â9-62">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>

         </div> 
        </div></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_churches">Other churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sinlessness_of_Mary" title="Sinlessness of Mary">Sinlessness of Mary</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Eastern Orthodoxy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Eastern Orthodoxy never accepted Augustine's specific ideas on original sin, and in consequence did not become involved in the later developments that took place in the Roman Catholic Church, including the Immaculate Conception.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuckin2012unpaginated_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuckin2012unpaginated-63">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoyle199636_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoyle199636-64">[62]</a></sup> The Eastern Orthodox do have a <a href="/wiki/Conciliarity" title="Conciliarity">conciliar</a> teaching on the matter, however. The <a href="/wiki/Synod_of_Jerusalem_(1672)" title="Synod of Jerusalem (1672)">Synod of Jerusalem (1672)</a> in its sixth decree teaches the existence of original sin ("hereditary sin flowed to his [Adam's] posterity; so that everyone who is born after the flesh bears this burden") but explicitly rejected the Augustinian notion of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Inherited_guilt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Inherited guilt (page does not exist)">inherited guilt</a> ("[by] this burden we do not understand [actual] sin").The decree continues in stating that "many both of the Forefathers and of the Prophets, and vast numbers of others...especially the Mother of God the Word, the ever-virgin Mary" experienced "only what the Divine Justice inflicted upon man as a punishment for the [original] transgression, such as sweats in labor, afflictions, bodily sicknesses...and lastly, bodily death."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When in 1894 Pope <a href="/wiki/Leo_XIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Leo XIII">Leo XIII</a> addressed the Eastern church in his encyclical <i>Praeclara gratulationis</i>, Ecumenical Patriarch Anthimos in 1895 replied with an encyclical approved by the Constantinopolitan Synod in which he stigmatised the dogmas of the Immaculate Conception and papal infallibility as "Roman novelties" and called on the Roman church to return to the faith of the early centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeyendorff198190_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeyendorff198190-8">[6]</a></sup> Some Eastern Orthodox have taken a more conciliatory view, an example being one popular <a href="/wiki/Ecumenist" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecumenist">ecumenist</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> Eastern Orthodox bishop, Kallistos Ware commenting that "the Latin dogma seems to us not so much erroneous as superfluous."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare199577_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare199577-67">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oriental_Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodoxy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Oriental Orthodoxy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Eritrean and Ethiopian Orthodox Tewahedo tradition affirms the Immaculate Conception. The <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Orthodox_Tewahedo_Church" title="Ethiopian Orthodox Tewahedo Church">Ethiopian Orthodox Tewahedo Church</a> celebrates the Feast of the Immaculate Conception on Nehasie 7 (August 13).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> The 96th chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Kebra_Nagast" title="Kebra Nagast">Kebra Nagast</a> states: âHe cleansed Eve's body and sanctified it and made for it a dwelling in her for Adamâs salvation. She [i.e., Mary] was born without blemish, for He made her pure, without pollution, and she redeemed his debt without carnal union and embrace...Through the transgression of Eve we died and were buried, and by the purity of Mary we receive honour, and are exalted to the heights.â </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Catholics">Old Catholics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Old Catholics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the mid-19th century some Catholics who were unable to accept the doctrine of papal infallibility left the Roman Church and formed the <a href="/wiki/Old_Catholic_Church" title="Old Catholic Church">Old Catholic Church</a>; their movement rejects the Immaculate Conception.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHillerbrand201263_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHillerbrand201263-70">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmit201914,_53_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmit201914,_53-71">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestantism">Protestantism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Protestantism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Protestants overwhelmingly condemned the promulgation of <i>Ineffabilis Deus</i> as an exercise in papal power, and the doctrine itself as without foundation in Scripture,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerringer2019507_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerringer2019507-7">[5]</a></sup> for it denied that all had sinned and rested on a translation of Luke 1:28 (the "full of grace" passage) that the original Greek did not support.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHammond2003601_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHammond2003601-72">[70]</a></sup> With the exception of some Lutherans and Anglicans, most Protestants therefore teach that Mary was a sinner saved through grace like all believers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGerman2001596_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGerman2001596-37">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Lutheranism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> showed an abiding devotion to Mary, including her sinlessness and sanctity, and Lutherans hold Mary in high esteem,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> but the Immaculate Conception does not hold the status of a dogma within Lutheranism.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> The ecumenical <i>Lutheran-Catholic Statement on Saints, Mary</i>, issued in 1990 after seven years of study and discussion, affirmed "that the Catholic teaching about the saints and Mary as set forth in the documents of Vatican II does not promote idolatrous belief or practice and is not opposed to the gospel," but conceded that Lutherans and Catholics remained separated "by differing views on matters such as the invocation of saints, the Immaculate Conception and the Assumption of Mary."<sup id="cite_ref-Ryan1990_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ryan1990-75">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglican_Communion">Anglican Communion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Anglican Communion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The final report of the <a href="/wiki/Anglican%E2%80%93Roman_Catholic_International_Commission" title="AnglicanâRoman Catholic International Commission">AnglicanâRoman Catholic International Commission</a> (ARCIC), created in 1969 to further ecumenical progress between the Roman Catholic Church and the Anglican Communion, recorded the disagreement of the Anglicans with the doctrine, although <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Catholic">Anglo-Catholics</a> may hold the Immaculate Conception as an optional pious belief.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmentrout2000260_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmentrout2000260-76">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mary_in_Islam" title="Mary in Islam">Mary in Islam</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkey.Konya035.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Turkey.Konya035.jpg/220px-Turkey.Konya035.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Turkey.Konya035.jpg/330px-Turkey.Konya035.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Turkey.Konya035.jpg/440px-Turkey.Konya035.jpg 2x" data-file-width="828" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkey.Konya035.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Manuscript of <a href="/wiki/Maryam_(sura)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maryam (sura)">Chapter 19</a> (<i>SÅ«ratu Maryam</i>) from a 9th-century <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur'an">Qur'an</a>, Turkey
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A saying of Mohammad recorded in the 9th century by the Muslim scholar <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Bukhari" title="Muhammad al-Bukhari">Muhammad al-Bukhari</a> quotes the prophet saying that Satan touches all the descendants of Adam "except Mary and her child"; medieval Christian monks later used this passage to claim that the Quran supported the Immaculate Conception, with the result that Muhammad was even depicted in altarpieces between the 16th and 18th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGÃ¶le2016115_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGÃ¶le2016115-77">[75]</a></sup> Islam, however, lacks the concept of original sin: according to the Quran, Adam and Eve were immediately forgiven for this sin in Eden after their asking of forgiveness. Also, the Quran states in various positions that every soul is only responsible for its good and bad deeds. Which means, no one will be held accountable for a sin of another, even their parents or offspring. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKritzeck2015120_fn.25_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKritzeck2015120_fn.25-78">[76]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Immaculate_Conception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-Disambiguate-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Disambiguate_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Immaculate Conception of Mary in the womb of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anne" title="Saint Anne">her mother</a> is not to be confused with Mary's purity in the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_birth_of_Jesus" title="Virgin birth of Jesus">virgin birth of Jesus</a>. See Bromiley (1995), p.272.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Definition-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Definition_3-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The Virgin Mary was preserved entirely free from original sin from the instant of her conception through a special prevenient grace, received in view of the merits of her Son in anticipation of the Redemption." See Reynolds (2012), p.330.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
